It will skip policy resolution\n86: // if the cached policy is already at the revision specified in the repo.\n87: //\n88: // Returns whether the cache was updated, or an error.\n89: //\n90: // Must be called with repo.Mutex held for reading.\n91: func (cache *PolicyCache) updateSelectorPolicy(identity *identityPkg.Identity) (bool, error) {\n92: \tcache.Lock()\n93: \tcip, ok := cache.policies[identity.ID]\n94: \tcache.Unlock()\n95: \tif !ok {\n96: \t\treturn false, fmt.Errorf(\"SelectorPolicy not found in cache for ID %d\", identity.ID)\n97: \t}\n98: \n99: \t// As long as UpdatePolicy() is triggered from endpoint\n100: \t// regeneration, it's possible for two endpoints with the\n101: \t// *same* identity to race to update the policy here. Such\n102: \t// racing would lead to first of the endpoints using a\n103: \t// selectorPolicy that is already detached from the selector\n104: \t// cache, and thus not getting any incremental updates.\n105: \t//\n106: \t// Lock the 'cip' for the duration of the revision check and\n107: \t// the possible policy update.\n108: \tcip.Lock()\n109: \tdefer cip.Unlock()\n110: \n111: \t// Don't resolve policy if it was already done for this or later revision.\n112: \tif cip.getPolicy().Revision >= cache.repo.GetRevision() {\n113: \t\treturn false, nil\n114: \t}\n115: \n116: \t// Resolve the policies, which could fail\n117: \tselPolicy, err := cache.repo.resolvePolicyLocked(identity)\n118: \tif err != nil {\n119: \t\treturn false, err\n120: \t}\n121: \n122: \tcip.setPolicy(selPolicy)\n123: \n124: \treturn true, nil\n125: }\n126: \n127: // LocalEndpointIdentityAdded creates a SelectorPolicy cache entry for the\n128: // specified Identity, without calculating any policy for it.\n129: func (cache *PolicyCache) LocalEndpointIdentityAdded(identity *identityPkg.Identity) {\n130: \tcache.insert(identity)\n131: }\n132: \n133: // LocalEndpointIdentityRemoved deletes the cached SelectorPolicy for the\n134: // specified Identity.\n135: func (cache *PolicyCache) LocalEndpointIdentityRemoved(identity *identityPkg.Identity) {\n136: \tcache.delete(identity)\n137: }\n138: \n139: // Lookup attempts to locate the SelectorPolicy corresponding to the specified\n140: // identity. !exists {\n173: \t\t\t\tmissing = true\n174: \t\t\t\tbreak\n175: \t\t\t}\n176: \t\t}\n177: \t\t// Only check if 'cs' selects 'remoteID' if one of the authTypes is still missing\n178: \t\t// from the result\n179: \t\tif missing && cs.Selects(remoteID) {\n180: \t\t\tif resTypes == nil {\n181: \t\t\t\tresTypes = make(AuthTypes, 1)\n182: \t\t\t}\n183: \t\t\tfor authType := range authTypes {\n184: \t\t\t\tresTypes[authType] = struct{}{}\n185: \t\t\t}\n186: \t\t}\n187: \t}\n188: \treturn resTypes\n189: }\n190: \n191: // cachedSelectorPolicy is a wrapper around a selectorPolicy (stored in the\n192: // 'policy' field). It is always nested directly in the owning policyCache,\n193: // and is protected against concurrent writes via the policyCache mutex.\n194: type cachedSelectorPolicy struct {\n195: \tlock.Mutex // lock is needed to synchronize parallel policy updates\n196: \n197: \tidentity *identityPkg.Identity\n198: \tpolicy   atomic.Pointer[selectorPolicy]\n199: }\n200: \n201: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5@14bf8b70da6d30733726dd61ffc026d1ed2b187c/-/blob/pkg/policy/distillery.go%3FL1-200"}}}
